ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-1-levels-of-organization">UNIT 1: LEVELS OF ORGANIZATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-1-levels-of-organization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic-one">TOPIC ONE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-one" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; <strong>Define of terms used in Anatomy and Physiology</strong></p>
<p><strong>Anatomy</strong>: the word anatomy is derived from a Greek word Anatome meaning to cut up. It is the study of structures that make up the body and how those structures relate with each other.</p>
<p>The study of anatomy includes many sub specialties. These are Gross anatomy, Microscopic anatomy, Developmental anatomy and Embryology.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Gross anatomy studies body structure with out microscope. Systemic anatomy studies functional relationships of organs within a system whereas Regional anatomy studies body part regionally. Both systemic and regional approaches may be used to study gross anatomy</p>
<p>Microscopic anatomy (Histology) requires the use of microscope to study tissues that form the various organs of the body.</p>
<p>Physiology: the word physiology derived from a Greek word for study of nature. It is the study of how the body and its part work or function.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="homeostasis">Homeostasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#homeostasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When structure and function are coordinated the body achieves a relative stability of its internal environment called homeostasis / staying the same. Although the external environmental changes constantly, the internal environment of a healthy body remains the same with in normal limits.</p>
<p>Under normal conditions, homeostasis is maintained by adaptive mechanisms ranging from control center in the brain to chemical substances called hormones that are secreted by</p>
<p>various organs directly into the blood streams. Some of the functions controlled by homeostasis mechanisms are blood pressure, body temperature, breathing and heart rate.</p>
<p>Cell: The smallest independent units of life. All life depends on the many chemical activities of cells. Some of the basic functions of cell are: growth, metabolism, irritability and reproduction.</p>
<p>Tissue: tissue is made up of many similar cells that perform a specific function. The various tissues of the body are divided in to four groups. These are epithelial, connective, nervous and muscle tissue</p>
<p>Organ: - Is an integrated collection of two or more kinds of tissue that works together to perform specific function. For example: Stomach is made of all type of tissues</p>
<p>System: Is a group of organs that work together to perform major function. For example: Respiratory system contains several organs.</p>
<p>&gt; Level of structural organization of the body</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The human body has different structural levels of organization, starting with atoms molecules and compounds and increasing in size and complexity to cells, tissues, organs and the systems that make up the complete organism.</p>
<p><strong>Atoms molecules and compounds:</strong> - At its simplest level, the body is composed of atoms. The most common elements in living organism are carbon, hydrogen, oxygen, nitrogen phosphorus and sulfur.</p>
<p><strong>Cell:</strong> The smallest independent units of life. All life depends on the many chemical activities of cells. Some of the basic functions of cell are: growth, metabolism, irritability and reproduction.</p>
<p><strong>Tissue:</strong> tissue is made up of many similar cells that perform a specific function. The various tissues of the body are divided in to four groups. These are epithelial, connective, nervous and muscle tissue</p>
<p><strong>Organ:</strong> - Is an integrated collection of two or more kinds of tissue that works together to perform specific function. For example: Stomach is made of all type of tissues</p>
<p><strong>System:</strong> Is a group of organs that work together to perform major function. For example: Respiratory system contains several organs.</p>
<p><strong>Organism level:</strong> - The various organs of the body form the entire organism.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Anatomical Positions.</strong>
Anatomical positions are universally accepted as the starting points for positional references to the body. In anatomical position the subject is standing erect and facing the observer, the feet are together, and the arms are hanging at the sides with the palms facing forward.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Relative Directional terms</strong>
Standardized terms of reference are used when anatomists describe the location of the body part. Relative means the location of one part of the body is always described in relation to another part of the body.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Body parts Regions</strong>
The body can generally be described to have areas of:</p>
<p><strong>Axial body part:</strong> - It is the part of the body near the axis of the body. This includes head, neck, thorax (chest), abdomen, and pelvis.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Appendicular body part: - It is the part of the body out of the axis line. This includes the upper and lower extremities. It is customary to subdivide the abdominal area into nine regions or more easily in to four quadrants.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="body-planes-and-sections">Body planes and sections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#body-planes-and-sections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Body planes are imaginary surfaces or planes lines that divide the body in to sections. This helps for further identification of specific areas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sagittal-plane">Sagittal plane:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sagittal-plane" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Divides the body into right and left half.</p>
<p>Mid sagittal plane: - divides body into equal left and right halves.</p>
<p>Para sagittal plane: - divides body into unequal left and right</p>
<p>Frontal plane: - divides the body into asymmetrical anterior and posterior sections.</p>
<p>Transverse plane: - divides the body into upper and lower body section.</p>
<p>Oblique plane: - divides the body obliquely into upper and lower section.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Body Cavities</strong></p>
<p>The cavities of the body house the internal organs, which commonly referred to as the viscera. The two main body cavities are the larger ventral (anterior) and the smaller, dorsal (posterior) body cavity.</p>
<p>The ventral body cavity constitutes the thoracic cavity and the abdomino-pelvic body cavity.</p>
<p>The Thoracic cavity houses lung and heart. It is protected by the rib cage &amp; associated musculature and the sternum anteriorly. It consists of the right and left pleural cavities and mediastinum (the portion of tissues and organs that separates the left and right lung).</p>
<p>Abdomino-pelvic Cavity extends from the diaphragm inferior to the floor of the pelvis. It is divided into superior abdominal and inferior pelvic cavity by imaginary line passing at upper pelvis.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-3-anatomy-of-the-nervous-system">3.3 Anatomy of the Nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-3-anatomy-of-the-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Behaviour depends on rapid information travel and processing. The nervous system is the body's communication network, handling information just as the circulatory system handles blood. The basic components of the nervous system are living cells called neurons and glia.</p>
<p>Glia are cells that provide structure and insulation for neurons: neural "glue." While neurons are cells that receive, integrate, and transmit information, permitting communication in the nervous system.</p>
<p>Table: Glial Cells and Function</p>
<p>A "typical" neuron consists of a soma, or cell body; dendrites, which are feeler-like structures, specialized to receive information; and an axon, which is a long, thin fibre that transmits signals away from the soma to other neurons, or to muscles or glands.</p>
<p>The basic flow of information is as follows: the dendrite receives a signal, and the signal passes through the soma and down the axon to the dendrites of another neuron.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>For efficient neural transmission to take place, many axons are covered with an insulating material called myelin. Myelin sheaths speed up transmission of signals that move along axons. Multiple sclerosis is a myelin degeneration disease, causing loss of muscle control, etc. due to loss of transmission efficiency in the nervous system when the myelin sheaths deteriorate.</p>
<p>At the end of an axon, the terminal buttons are small knobs that secrete chemical messengers called neurotransmitters. When the signal gets to the end of the axon, it causes these chemical messengers to be released into the synapse, the junction of two neurons. The chemicals flow across the synapse and stimulate the next cell.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-bc2ec243.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg">
Figure: Structure of a Neuron source Kassin, S. (1998). Psychology, second edition. Upper Saddle River, NJ: Prentice Hall.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-4-action-potential">3.4 Action Potential<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-4-action-potential" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When a neuron is stimulated, channels in the cell membrane open briefly, allowing the positive ions outside the cell to flow into the electronegative inside. This shift in the electrical charge travels along the axon and is referred to as an action potential.</p>
<p>Either an action potential occurs, or it does not. Once an action potential is initiated, it goes full force. Absolute refractory period is the minimum length of time after an action potential during which another action potential cannot begin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-5-the-synapse-and-synaptic-transmission">3.5 The Synapse and synaptic Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-5-the-synapse-and-synaptic-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Synapse is the point at which the nerve impulse passes from one neuron to another one. Two neurons make up a synapse. The axon of the presynaptic neuron breaks up into minute branches,</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>6</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>which terminate in small swellings called synaptic knobs, or terminal buttons. Synaptic knobs are in close proximity to the dendrites and the cell body of the postsynaptic neuron. The space between them is the synaptic cleft. Ends of synaptic knobs have spherical synaptic vesicles containing, a neurotransmitter, which is released into synaptic clefts. Neurotransmitters are synthesized by nerve cells, actively transported along the axons and stored in the synaptic vesicles.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-d4736aa3.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Figure: from Davis, S.F., &amp; Palladino, J.J. (1997). Psychology, Davis 2nd edition. Upper Saddle River, NJ: Prentice Hall.</p>
<p>Neurons do not actually touch at a synapse; instead, they are separated by a microscopic gap between the terminal button of one neuron and the cell membrane of another neuronthe synaptic cleft.</p>
<p>Electrical signals can't jump this gap. Instead, the neuron that is sending the message across the gap (the presynaptic neuron) releases neurotransmitters into the synaptic cleft.</p>
<p>This occurs when the action potential gets to the terminal button and causes the synaptic vesicles (storage sacs for the neurotransmitter-exocytosis) in response to the action potential, diffuse across the synaptic cleft, and spill its contents into the synaptic cleft.</p>
<p>The neurotransmitters diffuse across the space where they find open receptor sites on the postsynaptic neuron. These sites recognize and respond to some neurotransmitters, but not to others.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-31797207.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-neurons-communicate">How Neurons communicate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-neurons-communicate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Their action is short lived. Immediately they have stimulated the postsynaptic neuron or effector organ, such as a muscle fiber, they are either</p>
<ul>
<li>inactivated by enzymes or</li>
<li>Taken back into the synaptic knob.</li>
</ul>
<p>When a neurotransmitter from the presynaptic neuron crosses the synapse, finds an appropriate receptor site on the postsynaptic neuron, and binds, a voltage change occurs. This voltage change in the postsynaptic neuron is not an all-or-none, the neuron will fire or it will not, kind of thing. Instead, it changes the probability or potential that the postsynaptic neuron will fire. This is, therefore, called a postsynaptic potential.</p>
<p>The postsynaptic potential can be <strong>excitatory</strong> or <strong>inhibitory</strong>. An excitatory potential makes the neuron more likely to fire and decreases the negativity of the inside of the neuron with respect to the outside.</p>
<p>An inhibitory postsynaptic potential increases the negativity of the inside of the neuron with respect to the outside, making it less likely to fire.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>One neuron may receive signals from thousands of other neurons, across thousands of different synapses. Each neuron must integrate the many signals arriving at the same time before it "decides" to fire. Excitatory Post Synaptic Potential together add up; enough can cause the cell's voltage to reach the threshold at which the action potential will begin.</p>
<p>Excitatory Post Synaptic Potentials and Inhibitory Post Synaptic Potentials may balance out, as well, and the neuron would remain at rest. thus, the state of the neuron is a weighted balance.</p>
<p>Thought occurs through the firing of millions of neurons in unison. Our perceptions, thoughts, and actions depend on patterns of neural activity in interconnected neurons that fire together or sequentiallyneural networks. The links in these networks are constantly changing, with synaptic pruning or the elimination of old or unused synapses playing a larger role than the creation of new synapses in the sculpting of neural networks. For example, the number of synapses in the human visual cortex begins to decline after the age of one year.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-405b8ebc.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg">
Figure3.4</p>
<p>Cross-sectional views of an axon. The right end of the top axon is at rest, with a negatively charged interior. An action potential begins when the ion channels open and sodium ions (Na1) enter the axon. In this drawing, the action potential would travel rapidly along the axon, from left to right. In the lower axon, the action potential has moved to the right. After it passes, potassium ions (K1) flow out of the axon. This quickly renews the negative charge inside the axon, so it can fire again.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Sodium ions that enter the axon during an action potential are pumped back out more slowly. Their removal restores the original resting potential.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-b88d7eb0.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-6-organization-of-the-nervous-system">3.6 Organization of the nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-6-organization-of-the-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-6-1-central-nervous-system">3.6.1 Central Nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-6-1-central-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Central Nervous System consists of the Brain and Spinal cord</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-overview-of-the-brain">a) Overview of the Brain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-overview-of-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Figure 3.25 This simplified drawing shows the main structures of the human brain and describes some of their most important features. (You can use the color code in the foreground to identify which areas are part of the forebrain, midbrain, and hindbrain.)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The Brain constitutes about one-fiftieth of the body weight and lies within the cranial cavity. The parts are</p>
<p>a) Cerebrum
b) Thalamus
c) hypothalamus
d) midbrain
e) pons
f) medulla oblongata
g) Cerebellum.</p>
<p>Diencephalon</p>
<p>Brain Stem</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-db65efde.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-10f6a1ee.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>

<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i. Cerebrum- its part of the Dicephalon and is the largest part of the brain &amp; occupies the anterior and middle cranial fossae.</p>
<p>Divided by a deep cleft, the longitudinal cerebral fissure, into right and left cerebral hemispheres, each containing one of the lateral ventricles.</p>
<p>Deep within the brain, the hemispheres are connected by a mass of white matter (nerve fibres) called the corpus callosum. Cerebral cortex is divided into lobes that have the same names as the cranial bones under which they lie:</p>
<p>a. frontal
b. parietal
c. temporal
d. occipital.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-1d99aa87.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p>ii. Diencephalon-Deep within the cerebral hemispheres there are groups of cell bodies called nuclei, which act as relay stations where impulses are passed from one neuron to the next in a chain. Important masses of grey matter include thalamus hypothalamus.</p>
<p>Thalamus. Consists of two masses of grey and white matter situated within the cerebral hemispheres just below the corpus callosum, one on each side of the third ventricle. Sensory input from the skin, viscera and special sense organs is transmitted to the thalamus before redistribution to the cerebrum.</p>
<p>Hypothalamus. Situated below and in front of the thalamus, immediately above the pituitary gland. It is linked to the posterior lobe of the pituitary gland by nerve fibers and to the anterior lobe by a complex system of blood vessels. It therefore controls output of hormones from the pituitary gland</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>iii. Brain stem consists of the Midbrain, Pons, cerebellum, Reticular formation and Medulla Oblongata.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-b2370bf0.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg">
Figure: Brain Stem</p>
<p>Midbrain- Situated around the cerebrum above and the pons below. It Consists of nuclei and nerve fibres (tracts) which connect the cerebrum with lower parts of the brain and with the spinal cord. The nuclei act as relay stations for the ascending and descending nerve fibres.</p>
<p>Pons- It is situated in front of the cerebellum, below the midbrain and above the medulla oblongata. It consists mainly of nerve fibers, which form a bridge between the two hemispheres of the cerebellum, and of fibers passing between the higher levels of the brain and the spinal cord.</p>
<p>Medulla oblongata- It extends from the pons above and is continuous with the spinal cord below. It is about 2.5 cm long and it lies just within the cranium above the foramen magnum. Its anterior and posterior surfaces are marked by central fissures.</p>
<p>Reticular formation- It is a collection of neurones in the core of the brain stem, surrounded by neural pathways which conduct ascending and descending nerve impulses between the brain and the spinal cord</p>
<p>Cerebellum-Situated behind the pons and immediately below the posterior portion of the cerebrum occupying the posterior cranial fossa. Ovoid in shape and has two hemispheres, separated by a narrow median strip called the vermis. Grey matter forms the surface of the cerebellum, and the white matter lies deeply.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-overview-of-the-meninges">b) Overview of the Meninges<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-overview-of-the-meninges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Meninges are tissue membranes that cover the brain and spinal cord. Meninges has three layers of tissue named from outside inwards; they are:</p>
<p>Dura Mater
Arachnoid Mater
Pia Mater.</p>
<p>Dura and arachnoid maters are separated by a potential space, the subdural space.</p>
<p>Arachnoid and pia maters are separated by the subarachnoid space, containing cerebrospinal fluid.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The Dura Mater</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-5ba73e00.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p>Dura mater - consists of two layers of dense fibrous tissue.</p>
<p>i. Outer layer takes the place of the periosteum on the inner surface of the skull bones and the inner layer provides a protective covering for the brain.
ii. Spinal dura mater forms a loose sheath round the spinal cord. It is an extension of the inner layer of cerebral dura mater and is separated from the periosteum of the vertebrae and ligaments within the neural canal by the epidural or extradural space, containing blood vessels and areolar tissue. Nerves entering and leaving the spinal cord pass through the epidural space</p>
<p>Arachnoid mater - Delicate serous membrane that lies between the dura and pia maters.</p>
<p>Separated from the dura mater by the subdural space, and from the pia mater by the subarachnoid space, containing cerebrospinal fluid.</p>
<p>Pia mater - Fine connective tissue containing many minute blood vessels it adheres to the brain, completely covering the convolutions and dipping into each fissure it Continues downwards surrounding the spinal cord.</p>
<p>c) Overview Of The Spinal Cord And Its Functions</p>
<p>The spinal cord is an elongated, almost cylindrical part of the central nervous system, which is suspended in the vertebral canal surrounded by the meninges and cerebrospinal fluid. The spinal cord is continuous above with the medulla oblongata and extends from the upper border of the atlas to the lower border of the first lumbar vertebra (L1). Its approximately 45 cm long in an adult male.</p>
<p>Spinal reflexes control activities of the SC that are independent of the brain. To facilitate these there are extensive neuron connections between sensory and motor neurons at the same or different levels in the cord.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The spinal cord is incompletely divided into two equal parts, anteriorly by a short, shallow anterior median fissure and posteriorly by a deep narrow septum, the posterior median septum.</p>
<p>The SC is composed of grey matter in the center surrounded by white matter supported by neuroglia.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-0aad7564.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
Figure: Spinal Cord Showing Nerve Roots On One Side.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reflex-arc">Reflex Arc<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reflex-arc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pathway that nerve impulses travel when a reflex is elicited. It has 5 essential parts:</p>
<p>a. Receptorsdetect a change (the stimulus) &amp; generate impulses.
b. Sensory neuronstransmit impulses from receptors to the CNS.
c. Central nervous systemcontains one or more synapses.
d. Motor neuronstransmit impulses from the CNS to the effector.
e. Effectorperforms its characteristic action.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-d3bfe634.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-7-peripheral-nervous-system">3.7 Peripheral Nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-7-peripheral-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is broadly categorized into two systems that is the Somatic and Autonomic systems. In addition, it consists of the spinal nerves and cranial nerves.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Most of Peripheral Nervous system nerves are mixed nerves</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Spinal Nerves: Named and grouped according to the vertebrae with which they are associated.</p>
<p>I. 8 cervical
II. 12 thoracic
III. lumbar
IV. sacral
V. 1 coccygeal.</p>
<p>In the cervical, lumbar and sacral regions the anterior rami unite near their origins to form plexuses before proceeding to supply skin, bones, muscles and joints of a particular area. Thus, these structures have a nerve supply from more than one spinal nerve and therefore damage to one spinal nerve does not cause loss of function of a region.</p>
<p>In the thoracic region the anterior rami do not form plexuses. The 5 large plexuses of mixed nerves the:</p>
<ul>
<li>cervical plexuses</li>
<li>brachial plexuses</li>
<li>lumbar plexuses</li>
<li>sacral plexuses</li>
<li>Coccygeal plexuses.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Cranial Nerves</p>
<p>i) Olfactory nerves (sensory) - Originate in the upper part of the mucous membrane of the nasal cavity. Function: the sense of smell.
ii) Optic nerves (sensory) - Originate in the retinae of the eyes. Function: sense of sight
iii) Oculomotor nerves (motor) - Arise from nerve cells near the cerebral aqueduct. They supply: extraocular and intraocular muscles that move the eyeball hence alternating the shape of the lens and pupil
iv) Trochlear nerves (motor) Arise from nerve cells near the cerebral aqueduct. Supply the superior oblique muscles of the eyes.
v) Trigeminal nerves (mixed): It is among the largest of the cranial nerves. Have three main branches. Ophthalmic nerves; sensory only supply the lacrimal glands,</p>
<p>This document is available on
 studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>conjunctiva of the eyes, forehead, eyelids, anterior aspect of the scalp and mucous membrane of the nose. Maxillary nerves; sensory only supply the cheeks, upper gums, upper teeth and lower eyelids. Mandibular nerves; both sensory and motor. Largest of the three divisions supply the teeth and gums of the lower jaw, pinnae of the ears, lower lip and tongue. motor fibres supply the muscles of mastication.</p>
<p>vi) Abduces nerves (motor) - Arise from a nuclei lying under the floor of the fourth ventricle. supply the lateral rectus muscles of the eyeballs.</p>
<p>vii) Facial nerves (mixed) - Arises from nerve cells in the lower part of the pons. Motor fibres supply the muscles of facial expression. Sensory fibers convey impulses from the taste buds in the anterior two-thirds of the tongue.</p>
<p>viii) Vestibulocochlear (auditory) nerves (sensory). 2 distinct sets of fibres Vestibular nerves arise from the semicircular canals of the inner ear and convey impulses to the cerebellum. Associated with the maintenance of posture and balance. Cochlear nerves originate in the organ of Corti in the inner ear convey impulses to the hearing areas in the cerebral cortex where sound is perceived.</p>
<p>ix) Glossopharyngeal nerves (mixed) - Arise from nuclei in the medulla oblongata. Motor fibres stimulate the muscles of the tongue and pharynx and the secretory cells of the parotid (salivary) glands. Sensory fibres convey impulses to the cerebral cortex from posterior third of the tongue, tonsils and pharynx taste buds in the tongue and pharynx. Are essential for the swallowing and gag reflexes</p>
<p>x) Vagus nerves (mixed) - Have a more extensive distribution than any other cranial nerves. Arise from nerve cells in the medulla oblongata and other nuclei, and pass down through the neck into the thorax and the abdomen. Form an important part of the parasympathetic nervous system. Motor fibres supply smooth muscles and secretory glands of the pharynx, larynx, trachea, heart, oesophagus, stomach, intestines, pancreas, gall bladder, bile ducts, spleen, kidneys, ureter and blood vessels in the thoracic and abdominal cavities. Sensory fibres convey impulses from the lining membranes of the same structures to the brain.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>xi) Accessory nerves (motor) Arise from cell bodies in the medulla oblongata and in the spinal cord. Supply the sternodeidomastoid &amp; trapezius muscles. Branches join the vagus nerves and supply the pharyngeal and laryngeal muscles.
xii) Hypoglossal nerves (motor) Arise from nuclei in the medulla oblongata. Supply the muscles of the tongue and muscles surrounding the hyoid bone and contribute to swallowing and speech.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-somatic-nervous-system">c) Somatic Nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-somatic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The somatic nervous system contains two major types of neurons (nerve cells):</p>
<ul>
<li>Sensory neurons, also known as afferent neurons, are responsible for carrying information from the body to the CNS.</li>
<li>Motor neurons, also known as efferent neurons, are responsible for carrying information from the brain and spinal cord to muscle fibers throughout the body.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-e8757ed0.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg">
Figure: somatic nervous system</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-autonomic-nervous-system">d) Autonomic Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-autonomic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>ANS is divided into 2 divisions; having both structural &amp; functional differences.</p>
<p>i) Sympathetic (Thoraco-lumbar outflow)
ii) Parasympathetic (Cranio-sacral outflow).</p>
<p>They normally work in an opposing manner.</p>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)
Page 29 of 95</p>
<p>Sympathetic activity tends to predominate in stressful situations and parasympathetic activity during rest. Sympathetic is the part of the autonomic nervous system, located near the thoracic and lumbar regions in the spinal cord. Its primary function is to stimulate the body's fight or flight response. It does this by regulating the heart rate, rate of respiration, pupillary response and more.</p>
<p>Parasympathetic Autonomic Nervous System: It is located in between the spinal cord and the medulla. It primarily stimulates the body's "rest and digest" and "feed and breed" responses.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-4c6c8975.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg">
Figure 3.25</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-10-special-senses">3.10 Special senses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-10-special-senses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are five special senses:</p>
<p>i. Hearing
ii. Sight
iii. Smell
iv. Taste
v. Touch</p>
<p>Hearing, sight, smell and taste have specialized sensory receptors</p>
<p>a) Hearing and THE EAR</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The ear is the organ of hearing.</li>
<li>Supplied by cochlear part of 8th CN; stimulated by vibrations caused by sound waves.</li>
<li>Except the auricle (pinna), structures forming it are encased within petrous portion of the temporal bone</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure">Structure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>3 distinct parts:</li>
<li>Outer ear</li>
<li>Middle ear (tympanic cavity)</li>
<li>Inner ear.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-eca7398d.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="outer-ear-consists-of-auricle-external-acoustic-meatus">Outer ear - Consists of auricle &amp; external acoustic meatus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#outer-ear-consists-of-auricle-external-acoustic-meatus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The tympanic membrane (eardrum):</li>
<li>Completely separates external acoustic meatus from middle ear.</li>
<li>oval-shaped with slightly broader edge upwards</li>
<li>Formed by 3 types of tissue:</li>
<li>outer covering of hairless skin,</li>
<li>middle layer of fibrous tissue</li>
<li>Inner lining of mucous membrane continuous with that of middle ear.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="middle-ear-tympanic-cavity">Middle ear (tympanic cavity)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#middle-ear-tympanic-cavity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Irregular-shaped air-filled cavity within the temporal bone</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The cavity, its contents &amp; air sacs that open out of it are lined with either simple squamous or cuboidal epithelium.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Boundaries;</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Lateral wall; formed by tympanic membrane.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Roof and floor; formed by temporal bone.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Posterior wall; formed by temporal bone with openings leading to mastoid antrum through which air passes to air cells within the mastoid process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Medial wall; thin layer of temporal bone with 2 openings:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oval window</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Round window</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oval window is occluded by stapes &amp; round window, by a fine sheet of fibrous tissue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Three very small bones extending across middle ear from tympanic membrane to the oval window. Form a series of movable joints with each other &amp; with medial wall of the cavity at the oval window. Named according to their shapes.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>The malleus.</strong> Lateral hammer-shaped bone.</p>
<ul>
<li>Handle is in contact with tympanic membrane</li>
<li>Head forms a movable joint with incus.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>The incus.</strong> Middle anvil-shaped bone.</p>
<ul>
<li>Its body articulates with malleus, long process with stapes, and its stabilized by the short process, fixed by fibrous tissue to posterior wall of tympanic cavity.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>The stapes.</strong> Medial stirrup-shaped bone.</p>
<ul>
<li>Its head articulates with incus; its footplate fits into oval window. Held in position by fine ligaments.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-f1fe9f21.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Inner ear.</p>
<ul>
<li>Contains organs of hearing &amp; balance.</li>
<li>Two parts, <strong>bony labyrinth</strong> &amp; <strong>membranous labyrinth</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p>i) Bony labyrinth</p>
<ul>
<li>Cavity within temporal bone lined with periosteum.</li>
<li>Larger than, &amp; encloses, membranous labyrinth.</li>
<li>Between bony &amp; membranous labyrinth is a layer of watery fluid called <strong>perilymph</strong> and within membranous labyrinth is a watery fluid called <strong>endolymph</strong>.</li>
<li>Consists of:</li>
<li>1 vestibule</li>
<li>1 cochlea</li>
<li>3 semicircular canals.</li>
</ul>
<p>Vestibule: Is the expanded part nearest middle ear.</p>
<ul>
<li>Contains oval &amp; round windows in its lateral wall and two membranous sacs: <strong>utricle</strong> and <strong>saccule</strong> that are important in balance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cochlea: resembles a snail's shell.</p>
<ul>
<li>Has a broad base where it is continuous with the vestibule &amp; a narrow apex, &amp; it spirals round a central bony column.</li>
</ul>
<p>Semicircular canals: these are three tubes arranged so that one is situated in each of the three planes of space.</p>
<ul>
<li>Continuous with vestibule.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Membranous labyrinth</p>
<ul>
<li>Contains endolymph &amp; lies within its bony counterpart.</li>
<li>Comprises:</li>
<li>Vestibule; contains utricle &amp; saccule</li>
<li>Cochlea</li>
<li>3 semicircular canals.</li>
</ul>
<p>The cochlea</p>
<ul>
<li>Contains 3 compartments: the</li>
<li>Scala vestibuli</li>
<li>Scala media, or cochlear duct</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Scala tympani.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In cross-section, bony cochlea has 2 compartments containing perilymph:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scala vestibuli; originates at oval window,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scala tympani; ends at round window.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The two compartments are continuous with each other.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-d3318232.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<p>b) Sense Of Sight</p>
<ul>
<li>Organ of sight</li>
<li>Situated in orbital cavity and supplied by optic nerve (2nd CN).</li>
<li>Almost spherical in shape; about 2.5 cm in diameter.</li>
<li>Space between eye &amp; orbital cavity; occupied by adipose tissue.</li>
<li>Bony walls of orbit &amp; fat; protect the eye from injury.</li>
<li>The two eyes are structurally separate but some of their activities are coordinated so that they function as a pair.</li>
<li>Three layers of tissue in their walls. Outer fibrous layer: sclera &amp; cornea middle vascular layer or uveal tract: choroid, ciliary body &amp; iris inner nervous tissue layer: retina.</li>
</ul>
<p>Structures inside the eyeball lens,
Aqueous fluid (humour)
Vitreous body (humour).</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-29a75707.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sclera-and-cornea">Sclera and Cornea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sclera-and-cornea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sclera or white of the eye forms the outermost layer of tissue of posterior &amp; lateral aspects of eyeball</li>
<li>Consists of a firm fibrous membrane that maintains eyes shape &amp; gives attachment to extraocular/extrinsic muscles of eye</li>
<li>Anteriorly continues as a clear transparent epithelial membrane known as the cornea.</li>
<li>Light rays pass through the cornea to reach the retina.</li>
<li>Cornea is convex anteriorly and is involved in refracting (bending) light rays to focus them on retina.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="choroid">Choroid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#choroid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lines posterior 5/6 of inner surface of sclera.</li>
<li>Very rich in blood vessels and deep chocolate brown in colour. Light enters the eye through the pupil, stimulates nerve endings in the retina; then absorbed by the choroid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ciliary-body">Ciliary body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ciliary-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the anterior continuation of choroid consisting of ciliary muscle (smooth muscle fibres) &amp; secretory epithelial cells.</li>
<li>Gives attachment to suspensory ligament of the lens</li>
<li>Its Contraction &amp; relaxation changes the thickness of lens which refracts light rays entering the eye to focus them on the retina.</li>
<li>Epithelial cells secrete aqueous fluid into anterior segment of eye and cornea (anterior &amp; posterior chambers).</li>
<li>It is Supplied by parasympathetic branches of 3rd CN and Stimulation causes contraction of smooth muscle &amp; accommodation of the eye</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="iris">Iris<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Visible coloured part of eye</li>
<li>Extends anteriorly from ciliary body, lying behind cornea and in front of lens.</li>
<li>It divides anterior segment of eye into anterior &amp; posterior chambers, which contain aqueous fluid secreted by the ciliary body.</li>
<li>Its circular body is composed of pigment cells &amp; 2 layers of smooth muscle fibres, one circular &amp; the other radiating</li>
<li>In the center is an aperture known as the pupil.</li>
<li>It is Supplied by</li>
<li>Parasympathetic nerves which constricts pupil</li>
<li>Sympathetic nerves which dilates pupil.</li>
<li>Its color is genetically determined &amp; depends on the number of pigment cells present.</li>
<li>Albinos have no pigment cells</li>
<li>People with blue eyes have fewer than those with brown eyes.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-e337dc3e.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-d952d124.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lens">Lens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Highly elastic circular biconvex body, lying immediately behind the pupil.</li>
<li>Consists of fibres enclosed within a capsule</li>
<li>Suspended from ciliary body by suspensory ligament.</li>
<li>Its thickness is controlled by ciliary muscle through the suspensory ligament.</li>
<li>Refracts light rays reflected by objects in front of eye.</li>
<li>It is the only structure in the eye that can vary its refractory power; achieved by changing its thickness.</li>
<li>When the ciliary muscle contracts, it moves forward, releasing its pull on the lens, increasing its thickness.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The nearer is the object being viewed, the thicker the lens becomes to allow focusing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="retina">Retina<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#retina" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Innermost layer of the wall of eye</li>
<li>Extremely delicate structure and is well adapted for stimulation by light rays.</li>
<li>Composed of several layers of nerve cell bodies &amp; their axons, lying on a pigmented layer of epithelial cells, which attach it to the choroid.</li>
<li>The light sensitive layer consists of sensory receptor cells: <strong>rods &amp; cones</strong> that contain photosensitive pigments that convert light rays into nerve impulses</li>
<li>It lines about three-quarters of eyeball &amp; thickest at the back &amp; thins out anteriorly to end just behind the ciliary body.</li>
<li>Near the centre of posterior part is <strong>macula lutea</strong>, or <strong>yellow spot</strong>. Here, there is a little depression called <strong>fovea centralis</strong>, consisting of only <strong>cones</strong></li>
<li>Towards the anterior part of retina, there are fewer cone- than rod-shaped cells.</li>
<li>About <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.5\mathrm{cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> to the nasal side of macula lutea all, the nerve fibers of the retina converge to form the <strong>optic nerve</strong>.</li>
<li>Small area of retina where the optic nerve leaves the eye is <strong>optic disc</strong> or <strong>blind spot</strong> and has no light sensitive cells.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interior-of-the-eye">Interior of the eye<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interior-of-the-eye" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Anterior segment</strong> of the eye (space between the cornea and the lens) is incompletely divided into <strong>anterior</strong> &amp; <strong>posterior</strong> chambers by <strong>iris</strong>.</li>
<li>Both chambers contain a clear aqueous fluid (humour) secreted into the posterior chamber by ciliary glands.</li>
<li>Circulates in front of lens, through the pupil into the anterior chamber &amp; returns to the venous circulation through <strong>scleral venous sinus (canal of Schlemm)</strong> in the angle between the iris &amp; cornea.</li>
<li>Aqueous fluid supplies nutrients &amp; removes waste from transparent structures in the front of eye that have no blood supply, i.e. cornea, lens &amp; lens capsule.</li>
<li>Behind the lens &amp; filling posterior segment (cavity) of the eyeball is vitreous body (humour).</li>
<li>Soft, colorless, transparent, jelly-like substance composed of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>99</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">99\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">99%</span></span></span></span></span> water, some salts &amp; mucoprotein.</li>
<li>Maintains sufficient intraocular pressure to support the retina against the choroid &amp; prevent the eyeball walls from collapsing.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The eye keeps its shape because of the intraocular pressure exerted by the vitreous body &amp; aqueous fluid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-sense-of-smell">c) Sense of SMELL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-sense-of-smell" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nasal cavity has a dual function: a passageway for respiration and sense of smell (olfaction). Sensory nerves of smell originates from chemoreceptors in the mucous membrane of the roof of the nasal cavity above the superior nasal conchae</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-2a504ad6.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="figure-olfactory-structures">Figure; Olfactory Structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#figure-olfactory-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>All odorous materials give off volatile molecules, which are carried into the nose with the inhaled air and stimulate the olfactory chemoreceptors when dissolved in mucus.</li>
<li>The air entering the nose is warmed and convection currents carry eddies of inspired air to the roof of the nasal cavity.</li>
<li>'Sniffing' concentrates volatile molecules in the roof of the nose. This increases the number of olfactory receptors stimulated and thus the perception of the smell.</li>
<li>Inflammation of the nasal mucosa prevents odorous substances from reaching the olfactory area of the nose, causing loss of the sense of smell (anosmia). The usual cause is the common cold.</li>
<li>Adaptation. When an individual is continuously exposed to an odour, perception of the odour decreases and ceases within a few minutes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-sense-of-taste">d) Sense of TASTE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-sense-of-taste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Also .known as Gustation. It is closely linked with olfaction and it involves stimulation of chemoreceptors by dissolved chemicals. Taste buds contain chemoreceptors that are found on the papillae of the tongue and widely distributed in the epithelia of the tongue, soft palate, pharynx and the epiglottis. They consist of small sensory nerve endings of the glossopharyngeal, facial and vagus nerves (cranial nerves VII, IX and X). Some of the cells have hair-like microvilli on their free border, projecting towards tiny pores in the epithelium. Chemicals that enter the pores dissolved in saliva stimulate the sensory receptors</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-92a11992.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg">
Figure; structure of taste buds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="activity">Activity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-10-endocrine-system">3.10 Endocrine System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-10-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Consists of glands widely separated from each other with no direct anatomical links.</li>
<li>Endocrine glands - Consist of groups of secretory cells surrounded by an extensive network of capillaries, which facilitates diffusion of hormones from the secretory cells into the bloodstream. They are ductless because the hormones are secreted and diffuse directly into the bloodstream.</li>
<li>A hormone is formed in one organ or gland and carried in the blood to another organ (target organ or tissue), where it influences cellular activity, especially growth and metabolism.</li>
<li>Most hormones are synthesized from amino acids (amines, polypeptides and proteins; or are cholesterol-based lipids (steroids)).</li>
<li>Endocrine glands are:</li>
<li>1 pituitary gland</li>
<li>1 thyroid gland</li>
<li>4 parathyroid glands</li>
<li>2 adrenal (suprarenal) glands</li>
<li>the pancreatic islets (islets of Langerhans)</li>
<li>1 pineal gland or body</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>1 thymus gland</li>
<li>2 ovaries in the female</li>
<li>2 testes in the male.</li>
</ul>
<p>Copyright  The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. Permission required for reproduction or display.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-endocrine-system">The Endocrine System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-endocrine-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-bf196bbe.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-pituitary-gland">i) Pituitary Gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-pituitary-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>They act as a unit, regulating the activity of most of the other endocrine glands. Pituitary gland (Hypophysis) lies in the hypophyseal fossa of the sphenoid bone below the hypothalamus, to which it is attached by a stalk. It is Pea-sized, weighs about 500 mg &amp; consists of three distinct parts that originate from different types of cells.</p>
<ul>
<li>Anterior pituitary (adenohypophysis) is an upgrowth of glandular epithelium from the pharynx</li>
<li>Posterior pituitary (neurohypophysis) is a downgrowth of nervous tissue from the brain.</li>
<li>A network of nerve fibres exists between the hypothalamus and the posterior pituitary. Intermediate lobe; a thin strip between the 2 lobes</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Under the influence of hypothalamus, the anterior pituitary secrets</p>
<p>a) Thyroid stimulating hormone (TSH) stimulates growth and activity of thyroid gland and secretion of T and T
b) Growth hormone which regulates metabolism, promotes tissue growth bones and muscles
c) Adrenocorticotropic hormone (corticotrophin, ACTH) Stimulates the adrenal cortex to secret glucocorticoids
d) Prolactin stimulates milk production in the breast
e) Gonadotrophins ie Follicle stimulating Hormone-stimulates production of sperm in the testes, stimulates secretion of estrogen by the ovaries &amp; Luteinizing hormone- Secretion of testosterone by the testes, stimulates secretion of progesterone by the corpus luteum</p>
<p>The Posterior pituitary secrets</p>
<ul>
<li>Releases oxytocin and ant diuretic hormone (ADH or vasopressin); hormones synthesized in the hypothalamus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Oxytocin - Stimulates 2 target tissues during and after parturition (childbirth): uterine smooth muscle and the muscle cells of the lactating breast. During parturition, increasing amounts of oxytocin are released into the bloodstream in response to increasing distension of sensory stretch receptors in the uterine cervix by the baby's head.</p>
<p>Anti-diuretic Hormones (ADH) or vasopressin- to reduce urine output. Increases the permeability to water of the distal convoluted and collecting tubules of the nephrons of the kidneys. As a result, the reab-sorption of water from the glomerular filtrate is increased. Amount of ADH secreted is influenced by the osmotic pressure of the blood circulating to the osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus.</p>
<p>As the osmotic pressure rises, the secretion of ADH increases. More water is therefore reabsorbed and the urine output is reduced, thus the body retains more water and the rise in osmotic pressure is reversed.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-1-introduction">4.1 Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-1-introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-2-objectives-of-the-topic">4.2 Objectives of the topic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-2-objectives-of-the-topic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this topic, you should be able to:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-4-systems-involved-in-transport">UNIT 4; SYSTEMS INVOLVED IN TRANSPORT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-4-systems-involved-in-transport" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Divided into two;</p>
<ol>
<li>Cardiovascular system</li>
<li>Lymphatic system</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-1-cardiovascular-system">4.1; Cardiovascular system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-1-cardiovascular-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ul>

<li>Describe blood</li>
<li>Understand the heart</li>
